  <raw>MOTOR SPARES



MOTOR SPARES
Have South Africans missed out again?
TATA has announced that it will build a bus assembly plant in Mombasa, Kenya. The plant will assemble between 10 and 60 buses a month, mainly for the central African region. The plant will commence operations next year.
BMW, Mercedes join forces
IT HAS been expected for some time now that BMW and Mercedes-Benz would be forced into co-operation to compete against the mighty internal power of the Volkswagen/Audi group and Toyota/Lexus, but now it has been confirmed. Spokesmen for both companies have said discussions are under way regarding collaboration on development and production of parts.
Ford to cut down on Volvos
PARENT company Ford is cutting production at its Swedish luxury brand Volvo in a bid to cut losses. Ford executives have confirmed to the Wall Street Journal that CEO Alan Mulally is implementing a new business plan to return Volvo to profitability ahead of its eventual sale.
Toyota flies into jet business
FOLLOWING the launch of the new Honda Jet, Toyota is now looking at partnering with Mitsubishi on a new Japanese-built aircraft. Already under development the Mitsubishi Regional Jet will be a twin engine aircraft seating 70-90 people and will go on sale in 2012.
Ford SA adds railway siding
FORD Motor Company SA has opened its own railway siding to assist in transportation services as it expands its local manufacturing ahead of the new global pickup export programme. The siding will allow greater efficiency, says Ford, and direct transport to Silverton from Port Elizabeth.
Nissan plays green catch-up
NISSAN has announced it plans to begin mass production of lithium-ion batteries next year in a bid to become more involved in the low-emission vehicle market. Initial production will be 13000 batteries a year, but the company plans to increase this to 65000 by 2011. Many of these will be for Nissan electric vehicles, initially only for the US market.
Reports:</raw>
